                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">صَلَوْتُهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">صَلَوْتُ الظَّهْرَ</foreign>, (M,) <hi rend="ital">I struck,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beat, that part,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of him,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">of the back, which is called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَلًا</foreign>: (M:) or <hi rend="ital">I hit that part</hi> (M, K) with a thing, or with an arrow or some other thing: on the authority of Lh, who says that it is of the dial. of Hudheyl: and one says also <foreign lang="ar">صَلَيْتُهُ</foreign>; which is extr. [with respect to derivation], unless it be an instance of interchangeableness [of <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>]. (M.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">صَلِيَتْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">صَلَتْ</foreign>, said of a mare, or she-camel: see 4.    </entryFree>26:T1be8,<entryFree id="n24818" key="صلّى" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">صلّى</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M, K,) quasi-inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةٌ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">صَلٰوة</foreign>, for which one should not say <foreign lang="ar">تَصْلِيَةٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) or the latter is allowable as agreeable with rule and as occurring in old poetry, (MF, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He prayed, supplicated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">petitioned:</hi> (S, M, K:) and [particularly] <hi rend="ital">he performed the divinely-appointed act</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of prayer commonly</hi>] <hi rend="ital">termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاة</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">صَلٰوة</foreign>. (S.) Hence, in the Kur [ix. 104], (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">وَصَلِّ عَلَيْهِمْ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And pray thou for them.</hi> (Msb, TA.) <foreign lang="ar">صَلَّى عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٍ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">He prayed for such a one, and praised him.</hi> (TA.) And hence the verse of ElAashà cited in art. <foreign lang="ar">رسم</foreign>, conj. 8. (S, Mgh, * TA.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ دُعِىَ إِلَى وَلِيمَةٍ فَلْيُجِبْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَإِلَّا فَلْيُصَلِّ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Whoso is invited to a banquet,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a marriage-feast, let him comply, or, if not, let him pray</hi> for the inviter]. (M.) And the saying, in a verse of El-Aashà, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكِ مِثْلَ الَّذِى صَلَّيْتِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Keep thou to the like of thy prayer;</hi> i. e. he enjoined her to repeat the prayer for him: or, as some relate it, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكِ مِثْلُ الَّذِى صَلَّيْتِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">upon thee be the like of that for which thou hast prayed:</hi> (M:) these words he addressed to his daughter, on the occasion of her saying, “ O my Lord, ward off from my father diseases and pain. ” (Mgh.) The saying <foreign lang="ar">عَبِيدُ فُلَانٍ يُصَلُّونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The slaves of such a one perform the divinely-appointed act of prayer</hi>] means that they have attained to the age of virility. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">صلّى عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, said of an angel, means <hi rend="ital">He prayed for,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">begged, forgiveness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pardon, for him:</hi> and thus the verb sometimes means when said of other than an angel; as in the trad. of Sowdeh, in which it is said, <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا مِتْنَا صَلَّى لَنَا عُثْمَانُ بْنُ مَظْعُونٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">When we die, 'Othmán Ibn-Madh'oon will pray for forgiveness for us</hi>]; he having then died. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [And, said of a man, <hi rend="ital">He blessed him,</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">he invoked</hi> God's <hi rend="ital">blessing upon him;</hi> namely, the Prophet; or he said, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> (expl. by what here follows) accord. to the rendering of <foreign lang="ar">صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, i. e. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى النَّبِىِّ</foreign>, by Bd and others in the Kur xxxiii. 56.] One says, <foreign lang="ar">صَلَّيْتُ عَلَى النَّبِىِّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I blessed the Prophet;</hi> &amp;c.]. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And, said of God, <hi rend="ital">He blessed him,</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">He conferred blessing upon him:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">He had mercy on him:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">He magnified him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conferred honour upon him:</hi> hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى آلِ أَبِى أَوْفَى</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">O God, bless the family of Aboo-Owfà:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have mercy on</hi> &amp;c.: but in the saying [in the Kur xxxiii. 56], <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ ٱللّٰهَ وَمَلَائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِىِّ</foreign>, the verb does not import two meanings; for it has there only one meaning, which is “ magnification ” [i. e. these words mean <hi rend="ital">Verily God and his angels magnify the Prophet;</hi> or rather I would render them, <hi rend="ital">bless the Prophet,</hi> as this rendering implies magnification and also a meaning of the quasi-inf. n. given in the M and K, which is “ eulogy, ” or “ commendation, ” bestowed by God upon his apostle, while it imports God's “ conferring of blessing ” and the angels' “ invoking thereof ” ]: (Msb, TA:) [it is said that] <foreign lang="ar">اللّٰهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">O God, magnify Mohammad in the present world by exalting his renown and manifesting his invitation</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to ElIslám</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and rendering permanent his law, and in the world to come by accepting his intercession for his people and multiplying his reward:</hi> and it is disputed whether or not this form of prayer may be used for any but the Prophet [Mohammad]: El-Khattábee says that it may not, though he himself used it for others. (TA.) [<foreign lang="ar">صَلَّى ٱللّٰهُ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَسَلَّمَ</foreign> is a phrase commonly used by the Muslims after the mention of their prophet: see art. <foreign lang="ar">سلم</foreign>. See also <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةٌ</foreign> below.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">صلّى</foreign> said of a horse, (S, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَصْلِيَةٌ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">He followed next after the foremost</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in a race, at the goal</hi>]. (S, K.) Hence the saying [in a trad. of 'Alee], <foreign lang="ar">سَبَقَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَسُولُ ٱللّٰهِ وَصَلَّى أَبُو بَكْرٍ وَثَلَّثَ عُمَرُ</foreign> [expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">سبق</foreign>]. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">صلّى الحِمَارُ أُتُنَهُ</foreign>, (Sgh, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَصْلِيَةٌ</foreign>, (Sgh, TA,) <hi rend="ital">The</hi> [<hi rend="ital">wild</hi>] <hi rend="ital">ass drove together his she-asses, and made them to take the way</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that he would follow</hi>].                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">صَلًا</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">middle of the back</hi> of a human being and of any quadruped: (M, K:) and, (K,) or as some say, (M,) [app. in a beast,] the <hi rend="ital">part that slopes down from the hips,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">haunches:</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">space intervening between the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَاعِرَة</foreign> [app. meaning the <hi rend="ital">hinder projection of the haunch</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rump</hi> of a beast] <hi rend="ital">and the tail:</hi> (M, K:) or the <hi rend="ital">part on the right and left of the tail;</hi> (S, M, K;) the two together being called [the] <foreign lang="ar">صَلَوَانِ</foreign>, (S, K,) which is similarly expl. by Zj in relation to a she-camel; app. properly meaning the <hi rend="ital">two parts bordering upon the tail-bone:</hi> (TA:) or the <hi rend="ital">place in which is set the tail</hi> of the horse; dual as above: (Msb:) or the <hi rend="ital">bone upon which are the two buttocks:</hi> (Mgh: [there thus expl. in relation to a man:]) or the <hi rend="ital">bone in which is the place of setting of the tail-bone;</hi> thus expl. by IDrd: or the <foreign lang="ar">صَلَوَانِ</foreign> are the <hi rend="ital">two bones projecting from the two sides of the rump:</hi> or, accord. to some of the lexicologists, <hi rend="ital">two veins</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عِرْقَانِ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">in the place of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِدْف</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">in the rump</hi>]: (Ham p. 46:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">صَلَوَاتٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) an instance of a pl. formed by the addition of <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> from a masc. sing., (M,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَصْلَآءٌ</foreign>. (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ فِى أَصْلَائِهِمْ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I came at their rears.</hi> (TA.)    </entryFree>29:T190f,<entryFree id="n24821" key="صَلَاةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">صَلَاةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, or <foreign lang="ar">صَلٰوة</foreign>, [accord. to El-Hareeree, to be written with <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> when prefixed to a pronoun, and also in the dual number, (see De Sacy's Anthol.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n24821-1" target="مُصَلًّى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n24823"/></foreign> is said to have the same meaning. (Msb, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Then applied to signify <hi rend="ital">A certain well-known mode,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manner,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of religious service,</hi>] because comprising prayer; (Msb;) [the <hi rend="ital">divinelyappointed act of prayer;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one of the divinelyappointed</hi>

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n24821-2" target="مُصَلًّى" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n24823"/></foreign> is said to have the same meaning. (TA.) [The performance of this act is fully described in my work on the Modern Egyptians.] It is said to be, in this sense, a proper term of the law, not indicated by the language of the Arabs [before El-Islám] except as importing prayer, which is its primary signification: what Esh-Shiháb says respecting it necessarily implies its being a proper term of the law known to the Arabs [before ElIslám]: in the Mz it is said to be one of the words of El-Islám: but all of these sayings require consideration. (MF, TA, [Much more, which I omit as being unprofitable, is added on this point in the TA, partly from the Msb; as well as several different opinions respecting the derivation of the word as used in this sense, which are fanciful or absurd.]) The saying of the Prophet, <foreign lang="ar">لَا صَلٰوةَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِجَارِ المَسْجِدِ إِلَّا فِى المَسْجِدِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">There is no</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صلوة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">divinely-appointed act of prayer</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that is excellent</hi> or <hi rend="ital">complete</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to the neighbour of the mosque unless in the mosque</hi>].                   <foreign lang="ar">صلوة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">divinely-appointed prayer</hi>], or <hi rend="ital">the place thereof,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">is before thee,</hi>] alluding to that of sunset. (Mgh.) And he used the term <foreign lang="ar">الصَّلٰوةُ</foreign> as meaning <foreign lang="ar">سُورَةُ الصَّلٰوةِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَاتِحَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">Opening Chapter of the Kur-án,</hi> because it is a form of prayer, or] because the recital thereof is excellent, or satisfactory. (Mgh.) In the Kur xxii. 41, (I' Ab, S, M, Ksh, Bd,) [the pl.] <foreign lang="ar">صَلَوَاتٌ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Places of worship of the Jews:</hi> (I' Ab, S, M, Ksh, Bd, K:) said to be (Ksh, Bd) originally <foreign lang="ar">صَلُوتَا</foreign>, a Hebrew word, (Ksh, Bd, K,) arabicized: (Ksh, Bd:) this is the common reading of the word, and the most valid: other readings are <foreign lang="ar">صُلُوَاتٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">صُلَوَاتٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">صِلَوَاتٌ</foreign>; and beside these, some others which are perverted forms. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">Prayer for forgiveness</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pardon.</hi> (M, Mgh, K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [And <hi rend="ital">A blessing,</hi> as meaning <hi rend="ital">an invocation of</hi> God's <hi rend="ital">blessing</hi> upon any one.
